    1320                 :          0 :                 int                     precision = INTERVAL_PRECISION(typmod);
    1321                 :            : 
    1322                 :            :                 /*
    1323                 :            :                  * Our interpretation of intervals with a limited set of fields is
    1324                 :            :                  * that fields to the right of the last one specified are zeroed out,
    1325                 :            :                  * but those to the left of it remain valid.  Thus for example there
    1326                 :            :                  * is no operational difference between INTERVAL YEAR TO MONTH and
    1327                 :            :                  * INTERVAL MONTH.      In some cases we could meaningfully enforce that
    1328                 :            :                  * higher-order fields are zero; for example INTERVAL DAY could reject
    1329                 :            :                  * nonzero "month" field.  However that seems a bit pointless when we
    1330                 :            :                  * can't do it consistently.  (We cannot enforce a range limit on the
    1331                 :            :                  * highest expected field, since we do not have any equivalent of
    1332                 :            :                  * SQL's <interval leading field precision>.)
    1333                 :            :                  *
    1334                 :            :                  * Note: before PG 8.4 we interpreted a limited set of fields as
    1335                 :            :                  * actually causing a "modulo" operation on a given value, potentially
    1336                 :            :                  * losing high-order as well as low-order information.  But there is
    1337                 :            :                  * no support for such behavior in the standard, and it seems fairly
    1338                 :            :                  * undesirable on data consistency grounds anyway.  Now we only
    1339                 :            :                  * perform truncation or rounding of low-order fields.
    1340                 :            :                  */

    2091                 :            : int
    2092                 :            : timestamp_cmp_internal(Timestamp dt1, Timestamp dt2)
    2093                 :            : {
    2094                 :            : #ifdef HAVE_INT64_TIMESTAMP
    2095         [ #  # ]:          0 :         return (dt1 < dt2) ? -1 : ((dt1 > dt2) ? 1 : 0);
    2096                 :            : #else
    2097                 :            : 
    2098                 :            :         /*
    2099                 :            :          * When using float representation, we have to be wary of NaNs.
    2100                 :            :          *
    2101                 :            :          * We consider all NANs to be equal and larger than any non-NAN. This is
    2102                 :            :          * somewhat arbitrary; the important thing is to have a consistent sort
    2103                 :            :          * order.
    2104                 :            :          */
    2105                 :            :         if (isnan(dt1))
    2106                 :            :         {
    2107                 :            :                 if (isnan(dt2))
    2108                 :            :                         return 0;                       /* NAN = NAN */
    2109                 :            :                 else
    2110                 :            :                         return 1;                       /* NAN > non-NAN */
    2111                 :            :         }
    2112                 :            :         else if (isnan(dt2))
    2113                 :            :         {
    2114                 :            :                 return -1;                              /* non-NAN < NAN */
    2115                 :            :         }
    2116                 :            :         else
    2117                 :            :         {
    2118                 :            :                 if (dt1 > dt2)
    2119                 :            :                         return 1;
    2120                 :            :                 else if (dt1 < dt2)
    2121                 :            :                         return -1;
    2122                 :            :                 else
    2123                 :            :                         return 0;
    2124                 :            :         }
    2125                 :            : #endif
    2126                 :            : }

    2733                 :            :  *
    2734                 :            :  * Algorithm is per SQL92 spec.  This is much harder than you'd think
    2735                 :            :  * because the spec requires us to deliver a non-null answer in some cases
    2736                 :            :  * where some of the inputs are null.
    2737                 :            :  */

    2739                 :            : overlaps_timestamp(PG_FUNCTION_ARGS)
    2740                 :            : {
    2741                 :            :         /*
    2742                 :            :          * The arguments are Timestamps, but we leave them as generic Datums to
    2743                 :            :          * avoid unnecessary conversions between value and reference forms --- not
    2744                 :            :          * to mention possible dereferences of null pointers.

    2746                 :          0 :         Datum           ts1 = PG_GETARG_DATUM(0);
    2747                 :          0 :         Datum           te1 = PG_GETARG_DATUM(1);

    2752                 :          0 :         bool            ts2IsNull = PG_ARGISNULL(2);
    2753                 :          0 :         bool            te2IsNull = PG_ARGISNULL(3);
    2754                 :            : 
    2755                 :            : #define TIMESTAMP_GT(t1,t2) \
    2756                 :            :         DatumGetBool(DirectFunctionCall2(timestamp_gt,t1,t2))
    2757                 :            : #define TIMESTAMP_LT(t1,t2) \
    2758                 :            :         DatumGetBool(DirectFunctionCall2(timestamp_lt,t1,t2))
    2759                 :            : 
    2760                 :            :         /*
    2761                 :            :          * If both endpoints of interval 1 are null, the result is null (unknown).
    2762                 :            :          * If just one endpoint is null, take ts1 as the non-null one. Otherwise,
    2763                 :            :          * take ts1 as the lesser endpoint.
    2764                 :            :          */
    2765         [ #  # ]:          0 :         if (ts1IsNull)
    2766                 :            :         {
    2767         [ #  # ]:          0 :                 if (te1IsNull)
    2768                 :          0 :                         PG_RETURN_NULL();

    2770                 :          0 :                 ts1 = te1;
    2771                 :          0 :                 te1IsNull = true;

    3256                 :            :          * The above correctly handles the whole-number part of the month and day
    3257                 :            :          * products, but we have to do something with any fractional part
    3258                 :            :          * resulting when the factor is nonintegral.  We cascade the fractions
    3259                 :            :          * down to lower units using the conversion factors DAYS_PER_MONTH and
    3260                 :            :          * SECS_PER_DAY.  Note we do NOT cascade up, since we are not forced to do
    3261                 :            :          * so by the representation.  The user can choose to cascade up later,
    3262                 :            :          * using justify_hours and/or justify_days.
    3263                 :            :          */
    3264                 :            :         
    3265                 :            :         /*
    3266                 :            :          * Fractional months full days into days.
    3267                 :            :          *
    3268                 :            :          * Floating point calculation are inherently inprecise, so these
    3269                 :            :          * calculations are crafted to produce the most reliable result possible.
    3270                 :            :          * TSROUND() is needed to more accurately produce whole numbers where
    3271                 :            :          * appropriate.
    3272                 :            :          */

    3274                 :          0 :         month_remainder_days = TSROUND(month_remainder_days);
    3275                 :          0 :         sec_remainder = (orig_day * factor - result->day +
    3276                 :          0 :                                          month_remainder_days - (int) month_remainder_days) * SECS_PER_DAY;
    3277                 :          0 :         sec_remainder = TSROUND(sec_remainder);
    3278                 :            :         
    3279                 :            :         /*
    3280                 :            :          * Might have 24:00:00 hours due to rounding, or >24 hours because of time
    3281                 :            :          * cascade from months and days.  It might still be >24 if the combination
    3282                 :            :          * of cascade and the seconds factor operation itself.
    3283                 :            :          */

    3285                 :            :         {
    3286                 :          0 :                 result->day += (int) (sec_remainder / SECS_PER_DAY);
    3287                 :          0 :                 sec_remainder -= (int) (sec_remainder / SECS_PER_DAY) * SECS_PER_DAY;
    3288                 :          0 :         }
    3289                 :            :         
    3290                 :            :         /* cascade units down */
    3291                 :          0 :         result->day += (int32) month_remainder_days;
    3292                 :            : #ifdef HAVE_INT64_TIMESTAMP
    3293                 :          0 :         result->time = rint(span->time * factor + sec_remainder * USECS_PER_SEC);
    3294                 :            : #else

    3296                 :            : #endif
